Notes:
    The foundation to be cluster is highly unreliable
    The first problem seems to be the extremely slow response times.  less than 1000 operations per second.
    The second problem is that the cluster becomes unresponsive, even the `fdbcli` command running `status` will produce errors
        Although these errors are not consistent, sometimes the cluster comes back up
    As well, sometimes the cluster is up and properly running, but  testing shows zero operations per second
         Confirmed that the cluster is healthy with the `fdb analyze` command
            Although i get unknown data when running the `status` command
    Running more than 4 storageServersPerPod seems to be unreliable
        Although even running only 1 storageServersPerPod does not produce stable results either, but the cluster will come up
---

<A sample of the fdb status details output>

After watching the status details output for long enough, I noticed that io_timeout errors became more and more common, eventually overwhelming the processes, leaving only 1 or 2 processes without this error.

In the openshift_fdb_fails_over_time_io_timeout.png file you can see the total read/write speed slowly trend dowwards. There are some attempts at recovery, but ultimately the failures overload the server. The downward trend on this graph coorelates with the increase in io_timeout errors on the status details page

---
From this point on, we are using the new storage template, in this first test, I will put the details of the template down
---

The localstorage operator was used to create a new storageclass that should map nvme properly:

      volumeClaimTemplate:
        spec:
          storageClassName: fdb-nvme
          resources:
            requests:
              storage: {{volume_claim_storage}}
